## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Incident Debugging: Envoy Connection Pool Exhaustion

## Your Task

A production Envoy proxy is logging `upstream connect error or disconnect/reset before headers. reset reason: overflow`. Trace the error to its source in `envoyproxy/envoy`. Find: 1. The C++ source file that defines the `overflow` reset reason string. 2. The connection pool implementation files under `source/common/conn_pool/` or `source/common/http/` that trigger this overflow condition. 3. The configuration protobuf in `envoyproxy/data-plane-api` that controls `max_connections` and `max_pending_requests` circuit breaker thresholds.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive trace of the Envoy connection pool exhaustion error. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Discoveries

### 1. **Overflow Reset Reason Definition**
- Defined in `envoy/http/stream_reset_handler.h` as `StreamResetReason::Overflow`
- Also defined in `envoy/common/conn_pool.h` as `PoolFailureReason::Overflow`

### 2. **String Representation ("overflow")**
- Returned by `Utility::resetReasonToString()` in `source/common/http/utility.cc` (line 1030-1031)

### 3. **Overflow Triggering Points**
Two locations in `source/common/conn_pool/conn_pool_base.cc`:
- **Line 175**: Checks `resourceManager().requests().canCreate()` → "max streams overflow"
- **Line 282**: Checks `resourceManager().pendingRequests().canCreate()` → "max pending streams overflow"

### 4. **Error Message Construction**
Built in `source/common/router/router.cc` (lines 1415-1420):
```
"upstream connect error or disconnect/reset before headers. reset reason: overflow"
```

### 5. **Circuit Breaker Configuration**
Located in data-plane-api:
- **V3 (active)**: `envoy/config/cluster/v3/circuit_breaker.proto`
- **V2 (deprecated)**: `envoy/api/v2/cluster/circuit_breaker.proto`

Both define `CircuitBreakers.Thresholds` with:
- `max_connections` (default: 1024)
- `max_pending_requests` (default: 1024)
- `max_requests` (default: 1024)

### 6. **Resource Enforcement**
`ResourceManagerImpl` in `source/common/upstream/resource_manager_impl.h` enforces limits through `canCreate()` methods.
